  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1854884789" />
    <a title="Girish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5924440-girish"><img alt="Girish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591866419p2/5924440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1854884789?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Girish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Girish" href="/user/show/5924440-girish">Girish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1854884789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer107939489961667010">The first Jeeves-Wooster short story collection is akin to the wright brothers aircraft - surely a piece of genius but way ruddier than how you've grown to love them. My first audio book as well, this was a different experience.<br/><br/>The book is complete with all the buffoonery, muddled up scenarios, slapstick wit and wry English humor. A collection of 8 stories - 4 of which featuring Reggie Peppers who seems like the earlier version of Bertie, always trying to help his friends. Reggie Peppers is said</span>
  <span id="freeText107939489961667010" style="display:none">The first Jeeves-Wooster short story collection is akin to the wright brothers aircraft - surely a piece of genius but way ruddier than how you've grown to love them. My first audio book as well, this was a different experience.<br /><br />The book is complete with all the buffoonery, muddled up scenarios, slapstick wit and wry English humor. A collection of 8 stories - 4 of which featuring Reggie Peppers who seems like the earlier version of Bertie, always trying to help his friends. Reggie Peppers is said to have tried to steal Jeeves by offering twice the salary to add the connect.<br /><br />Needless to say, the Jeeves stories are more endearing. The stories are set in New York, where Bertie is hiding from Aunt Agatha after he failed to prevent his cousin Gussie from marrying a club dancer. Jeeves is more a direct Mr.Fixit in the stories where Bertie is the victim of a good heart. In the last story, Bertie vacates his house to help his friend Rocky keep up a lie to his aunt. The best story featuring Reggie is the one where he helps his friend figure out his angry wife's birthday. <br /><br />Some lovely quotes to go with. A fun read!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="107939489961667010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1147061843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1147061843" />
    <a title="Nathan Eaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10788585-nathan-eaton"><img alt="Nathan Eaton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522118407p2/10788585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1147061843?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan Eaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan Eaton" href="/user/show/10788585-nathan-eaton">Nathan Eaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10788585-nathan-eaton?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10788585-nathan-eaton?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10788585-nathan-eaton?shelf=short-stuff">short-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147061843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12645148313197055547">I was a bit worried about this one. I knew Wodehouse was always considered one of the great comedy writers. Two of my favorite authors (Douglas Adams and Terry Pratchett) both listed him as an influence to their work. There were plenty of signs that I shouldn't have worried. So why did I? Just a few reasons.<br/><br/>- Comedy doesn't generally seem to stand the test of time as well as other genres. I generally don't find older comedy films all that funny. I'll get some flack for this, but I didn't find An</span>
  <span id="freeText12645148313197055547" style="display:none">I was a bit worried about this one. I knew Wodehouse was always considered one of the great comedy writers. Two of my favorite authors (Douglas Adams and Terry Pratchett) both listed him as an influence to their work. There were plenty of signs that I shouldn't have worried. So why did I? Just a few reasons.<br /><br />- Comedy doesn't generally seem to stand the test of time as well as other genres. I generally don't find older comedy films all that funny. I'll get some flack for this, but I didn't find Animal House funny at all. And while I love Steve Martin, I just don't get The Jerk.<br /><br />- Can a middle-class American guy really relate to the stuffy British aristocrats? Furthermore, how funny can stuffy British Aristocrats be?<br /><br />- I generally don't like short story collections. After reading so many stories, it can become overbearing. I've also found that in short-story collections, you'll find the same story essentially written multiple times, just with different characters and settings.<br /><br />- I'd already heard so many good things, I just didn't think it could live up to it.<br /><br />Well, as it turns out, my apprehensions were unfounded. Wodehouse has been praised for his superior wit, and he deserves it. He is excellent at turns of phrase, and can make some dull subject matter supremely funny. His comedy writing is actually timeless. And his comedy timing is actually writing! His characters Jeeves and Wooster are fantastic.<br /><br />I'd definitely recommend this one to anyone who appreciates comedy. It's very likely a comedian you love has been inspired by Wodehouse, and you can see from where they drew it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12645148313197055547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3599298623" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3599298623" />
    <a title="Deacon Tom F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6526961-deacon-tom-f"><img alt="Deacon Tom F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601403557p2/6526961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3599298623?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deacon Tom F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deacon Tom F" href="/user/show/6526961-deacon-tom-f">Deacon Tom F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3599298623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15220361819070851846">A really nice book. <br/><br/>Jeeves is a great character. He always comes to the day when problems occur. It was very funny, even hilarious in places. <br/><br/>I certainly could use a Jeeves in my life. Oh, the pain of middle class....lol<br/><br/>The language is enchanting and caused me to use the dictionary more than I usually do. It is from 1919 though as well as being British. <br/><br/>I recommend. A fun book. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1030781982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1030781982" />
    <a title="Randee Baty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4474156-randee-baty"><img alt="Randee Baty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404683560p2/4474156.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1030781982?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Randee Baty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Randee Baty" href="/user/show/4474156-randee-baty">Randee Baty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18882232-my-man-jeeves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4474156-randee-baty?shelf=kindle-freebie">kindle-freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4474156-randee-baty?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4474156-randee-baty?shelf=british-comic-novel">british-comic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4474156-randee-baty?shelf=british-20th-century">british-20th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1030781982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10640314458489094135">Hugh Laurie states the case admirably "The first thing you should know, and probably the last, too, is that PG Wodehouse is still the funniest writer ever to have put words on paper." I couldn't agree more.<br/><br/>"I'm not absolutely certain of my facts, but I rather fancy it's Shakespeare-or, if not, it's some equally brainy lad-who says that it's always just when a chappie is feeling particularly top-hole and more than usually braced with things in general that Fate sneaks up behind him with a bit of </span>
  <span id="freeText10640314458489094135" style="display:none">Hugh Laurie states the case admirably "The first thing you should know, and probably the last, too, is that PG Wodehouse is still the funniest writer ever to have put words on paper." I couldn't agree more.<br /><br />"I'm not absolutely certain of my facts, but I rather fancy it's Shakespeare-or, if not, it's some equally brainy lad-who says that it's always just when a chappie is feeling particularly top-hole and more than usually braced with things in general that Fate sneaks up behind him with a bit of lead piping.. There's no doubt the man's right." And so is our first introduction to Bertie Wooster.<br /><br />Bertie Wooster seems destined to always have Fate sneaking up behind him with a lead pipe. If anything can go wrong for him, it will. Overbearing relatives, friends that need rescuing, ties that don't match the suit he's wearing. Enter Jeeves, his gentleman's gentleman. Calm, cool, and collected, Jeeves is always able to get Bertie and his friends out of whatever scrape they have gotten into. And he's always able to make sure that Bertie is properly attired while doing it. Comis genius is the only description of what goes on in a Jeeves story.<br /><br />This book, Wodehouse's earliest writings about Jeeves, is a set of short stories, several of them about Reggie Pepper, rather than Bertie. The two characters are almost interchangeable except for the absence of Jeeves in the Pepper stories. Some of these stories were rewritten for later Jeeves books.<br /><br />If you've never read P.G. Wodhouse before, his writing is almost hard to describe. He's quintessentially British. He's hilarious and there is plenty of slapstick humour but there is also lots of dry humour. His vocabulary is different than anyone else I've ever read. His use of the slang of the time and his depiction of the idle upper class and the aristocracy before WWII are just fun! He's one of the five authors who's works I would take to a desert island with me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10640314458489094135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_414270711" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/414270711" />
    <a title="Forrest" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/811928-forrest"><img alt="Forrest" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558621304p2/811928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/414270711?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Forrest" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Forrest" href="/user/show/811928-forrest">Forrest</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 0012566403" href="/book/show/9785447-my-man-jeeves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer414270711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8785153409693955313">It's P.G. Wodehouse, so why not five stars?<br/><br/>Well, here's the scoop. I love Bertie Wooster and Jeeves. One of the most clever duos to have ever graced the printed page. Between Jeeve's restrained resourcefulness and Bertie's self-admitted idiocy, there is a lot of potential for misadventure, and Wodehouse delivers it in droves. <br/><br/>Half of the short stories in this volume are Jeeves and Wooster material. The other half is from what I glean as earlier material, with a main character named Reggie Pepper</span>
  <span id="freeText8785153409693955313" style="display:none">It's P.G. Wodehouse, so why not five stars?<br /><br />Well, here's the scoop. I love Bertie Wooster and Jeeves. One of the most clever duos to have ever graced the printed page. Between Jeeve's restrained resourcefulness and Bertie's self-admitted idiocy, there is a lot of potential for misadventure, and Wodehouse delivers it in droves. <br /><br />Half of the short stories in this volume are Jeeves and Wooster material. The other half is from what I glean as earlier material, with a main character named Reggie Peppers. Now, Peppers is a fore-runner of Wooster, no doubt, but he is a bit of a homunculus, a shadow, a pretender, when compared to the sharp imbecility of Bertie Wooster. Peppers is . . . well, smarter. And more wordy. The clipped down anti-witticisms of Wooster are watered down in Peppers, which leaves the Peppers stories a little wanting. Peppers wants to be Wooster, but doesn't quite get there because, quite frankly, Peppers isn't dumb enough.<br /><br />I am so glad that Wodehouse decided to stick with it and followed through to give life to Bertie Wooster. This isn't to say that Wodehouse missed here. Peppers made an adequate character, but Wooster, with Jeeves as his foil, is pure stupid genius. The Wooster stories in <i>My Man Jeeves</i> bear this out. The merry bungling of Wodehouse's longer works is apparent and the plot lines are as ridiculous and convoluted as one can expect in short fiction (though not as ridiculous and convoluted as his novellas/novels). Five stars for Bertie, negative one star for Peppers. Still strongly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8785153409693955313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1097954541" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097954541" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097954541?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781453875063" href="/book/show/9792574-my-man-jeeves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097954541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14271657060644317935">This is the earliest collection of stories featuring Bertie Wooster and his extremely competent valet, Jeeves. Interestingly, Bertie Wooster is hiding out in New York, having failed to carry out an errand for his indomitable Aunt Agatha and unable to face returning home to face her possible wrath. During these stories, Wooster – or his friends – get into various scrapes and are saved by Jeeves. Often the plans backfire, in various farcical ways, but Jeeves always has a suggestion to help rescue </span>
  <span id="freeText14271657060644317935" style="display:none">This is the earliest collection of stories featuring Bertie Wooster and his extremely competent valet, Jeeves. Interestingly, Bertie Wooster is hiding out in New York, having failed to carry out an errand for his indomitable Aunt Agatha and unable to face returning home to face her possible wrath. During these stories, Wooster – or his friends – get into various scrapes and are saved by Jeeves. Often the plans backfire, in various farcical ways, but Jeeves always has a suggestion to help rescue the situation.<br /><br />Some of the stories in this collection feature another character – Reggie Pepper. He is very similar to Wooster and, again, much of the storyline concerns his friends problems. Often his attempts to help are less than welcome, or there is some confusion, but overall the entire collection is humorous and nicely realised. Short stories are difficult to write well, but Wodehouse is obviously a master of the form and these are a fun read and a good introduction to his characters.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14271657060644317935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7FzbNN6RQMcTt3bDwq0Q77Gssw4k7Md3aY7TgYUC8nTWerLmZc+Jr7ScwqI1WBowZ/NUxuphSRAy8JUwSEEA7g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CCAS/L/2elDcZioPGH6J8TnBNkXev7pFZ7toWko+eN0yBnsuBKizOHtNnm7vi4Mu757RjRAyNCI8xS7rh32KRw==')})
  }
//]]>

Wodehouse documented the lives of the inimitable Jeeves and Wooster for nearly sixty years, from their first appearance in 1915 (&quot;Extricating Young Gussie&quot;) to his final completed novel (Aunts Aren\'t Gentlemen) in 1974. These two were the finest creations of a novelist widely proclaimed to be the finest comic English writer by critics and fans alike.\n\nNow, forty years later, Bertie and Jeeves return in a hilarious affair of mix-ups and mishaps. With the approval of the Wodehouse estate, acclaimed novelist Sebastian Faulks brings these two back to life for their legion of fans. Bertie, nursing a bit of heartbreak over the recent engagement of one Georgina Meadowes to someone not named Wooster, agrees to &quot;help&quot; his old friend Peregrine &quot;Woody&quot; Beeching, whose own romance is foundering. That this means an outing to Dorset, away from an impending visit from Aunt Agatha, is merely an extra benefit. Almost immediately, things go awry and the simple plan quickly becomes complicated. Jeeves ends up impersonating one Lord Etringham, while Bertie pretends to be Jeeves\' manservant &quot;Wilberforce,&quot;—and this all happens under the same roof as the now affianced Ms. Meadowes.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7963.P_G_Wodehouse">About P.G. Wodehouse</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7963.P_G_Wodehouse"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1198684105p3/7963.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7963.P_G_Wodehouse">P.G. Wodehouse
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
5,401
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17827865548421493218">Sir Pelham Grenville Wodehouse, KBE, was a comic writer who enjoyed enormous popular success during a career of more than seventy years and continues to be widely read over 40 years after his death. Despite the political and social upheavals that occurred during his life, much of which was spent in France and the United States, Wodehouse's main canvas remained that of prewar English upper-class so</span>
  <span id="freeText17827865548421493218" style="display:none">Sir Pelham Grenville Wodehouse, KBE, was a comic writer who enjoyed enormous popular success during a career of more than seventy years and continues to be widely read over 40 years after his death. Despite the political and social upheavals that occurred during his life, much of which was spent in France and the United States, Wodehouse's main canvas remained that of prewar English upper-class society, reflecting his birth, education, and youthful writing career.<br /><br />An acknowledged master of English prose, Wodehouse has been admired both by contemporaries such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4025.Hilaire_Belloc" title="Hilaire Belloc" rel="nofollow noopener">Hilaire Belloc</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11315.Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh" rel="nofollow noopener">Evelyn Waugh</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6989.Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling" rel="nofollow noopener">Rudyard Kipling</a> and by more recent writers such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams" title="Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Douglas Adams</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3299.Salman_Rushdie" title="Salman Rushdie" rel="nofollow noopener">Salman Rushdie</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a>. Sean O'Casey famously called him "English literature's performing flea", a description that Wodehouse used as the title of a collection of his letters to a friend, Bill Townend.<br /><br />Best known today for the <i>Jeeves</i> and <i>Blandings Castle</i> novels and short stories, Wodehouse was also a talented playwright and lyricist who was part author and writer of fifteen plays and of 250 lyrics for some thirty musical comedies. He worked with Cole Porter on the musical <i>Anything Goes</i> (1934) and frequently collaborated with Jerome Kern and Guy Bolton. He wrote the lyrics for the hit song <i>Bill</i> in Kern's Show Boat (1927), wrote the lyrics for the Gershwin/Romberg musical <i>Rosalie</i> (1928), and collaborated with Rudolf Friml on a musical version of <i>The Three Musketeers</i> (1928).</span>
  <a data-text-id="17827865548421493218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

It is the only Jeeves novel in which his employer, Bertie Wooster, does not appear (though he is mentioned). In his absence he has allowed Jeeves to offer his services to William &quot;Bill&quot; Rowcester, the impoverished 9th Earl of Rowcester, whose stately home, Rowcester Abbey, is an encumbrance for which the Earl is seeking a buyer.           $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_18029').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_18029').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_18029').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
